  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_03db63a4-b1c8-4780-8fa7-2964fa210184'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer17249256868574262455">Elizabeth is a brilliant loner with a troubling secret she doesn't even know. As if the trauma of her mother being abducted before her eyes as a young girl wasn't enough, the small town she lives in thinks she’s crazy. That all changed when she met Michael, a mysterious and handsome man who identified with her like no one else before.<br/><br/>Michael’s long time friend Vincent visi</span>
  <span id="freeText17249256868574262455" style="display:none">Elizabeth is a brilliant loner with a troubling secret she doesn't even know. As if the trauma of her mother being abducted before her eyes as a young girl wasn't enough, the small town she lives in thinks she’s crazy. That all changed when she met Michael, a mysterious and handsome man who identified with her like no one else before.<br /><br />Michael’s long time friend Vincent visits and drops the bombshell of a lifetime on Elizabeth and her world becomes completely unraveled. Vincent’s information has revealed the world for what it is; a place where the impossible is real, and myths and legends walk slyly in shadow. A world that Elizabeth will learn she too is a member.<br /><br />Now, the three are caught up in a thousand year long conspiracy they never could have imagined. The three must rely on one another and the secret connection they all share if they have a chance to survive.</span>

<div id="review_786009316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/786009316" />
    <a title="Jade Lauron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13693671-jade-lauron"><img alt="Jade Lauron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350434659p2/13693671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/786009316?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jade Lauron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jade Lauron" href="/user/show/13693671-jade-lauron">Jade Lauron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13693671-jade-lauron?shelf=fever-pulp-fantasy">fever-pulp-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer786009316&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer786009316" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2014369534682394599">"The first and most important thing: forget everything you've heard or read. Forget everything you thought you knew."<br/><br/>Wow, what is that? The beginning lines they forced you to start with in your creative writing class? But I'm going to go with this, by first forgetting the opening lines to this book and giving it a fighting chance.<br/><br/>First, the dialogue: Moments of, dare I say, exceptional talent, intertwined with areas that could certainly use some tightening up. Still, it shows promise. I keep rea</span>
  <span id="freeText2014369534682394599" style="display:none">"The first and most important thing: forget everything you've heard or read. Forget everything you thought you knew."<br /><br />Wow, what is that? The beginning lines they forced you to start with in your creative writing class? But I'm going to go with this, by first forgetting the opening lines to this book and giving it a fighting chance.<br /><br />First, the dialogue: Moments of, dare I say, exceptional talent, intertwined with areas that could certainly use some tightening up. Still, it shows promise. I keep reading.<br /><br />The author displays total command of first-person narrative voice, none of that "yo-ismo" which is a term I learned in Spanish class about a millennium ago. It means the text isn't burdened down with "I's" and, to give the author his due, it's not even heavy on the "me's". What the author doesn't display is mastery of the thesaurus. The overall vocabulary seems limited; I wasn't sure if this was supposed to be Young Adult Fiction or not, but it definitely reads at about the eighth grade level. That's okay, because I like YA Fiction, at least, until we start coming across little gems like this one found at the beginning of Chapter Two:<br /><br />"He's funny and charming...and as much as I <i>really</i> hate to admit it, he's a pretty smart guy. I don't know him well enough to admit it..." *shudder*<br /><br />So far, it sounds like a decent book. So why did I downgrade it to nothing? Because this author has NO SENSE OF CONFLICT. Our heroes are pretty much the two most powerful creatures on earth, stomping around and kicking butt then entire time. Oh look, you have super speed, super strength, telepathic abilities, mind control, impervious skin, and you're immortal. Everything always goes according to plan, and no one double crosses anyone, or could, because everyone's too smart for that. I felt like I was watching someone play a video game after they'd turned on cheat mode.<br /><br />Sure, you've got a Twilight-style love triangle, which is sure to have the fan-fic crowd slobbering on your shoes, but did you have to set it up in such a way that not a single person is jealous of anyone else? The girl likes both guys, they're friends with each other, and both pretty much agree that whoever gets the girl, it's okay by the other one, "hey, we'll still be buds forever!" There wasn't even a paragraph of angst when they asked mom if it was okay to kill her evil son. Of course mom is going to agree, because, you know, her son is bad. What? <br /><br />Who wants to read a book in where your protagonist has the obvious advantage in all ways against a lesser force, and then wins? What's next, hero slays fencepost? I wasn't even tempted by book two, and I'm the queen of OCD completionism. In fact, I had to force myself to finish book one, because I knew what the ending was halfway through, the heroes had already planned it out and told us. And, as I expected, everything went just like clockwork.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2014369534682394599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4145131234643439771" style="display:none">This was a great book.. Truly addicting. I like that OL keeps all the supernaturals that we know and love but also introduces us to something new. A keeper is a new supernatural species to me along with other surprise's that OL adds in the book.<br /><br />Izzy has been trying to find out what took her mother and everyone thinks that she is crazy. Her father is no help since he has become a drunk. She has to see shrink after shrink since everyone thinks that she is crazy. Then she meets Michael.<br /><br />Michael is the first boy that she has ever been attracted to. They eventually start to become close and she tells him about her mother and he is the first person to believe her and not think that she is crazy. Then she meets Vincent.<br /><br />Vincent is rude and sarcastic and Izzy can't seem to figure out why she likes him. Along with meeting Vincent comes the truth. Michael has been keeping secrets and Vincent is all to willing to tell what those are. Michael is a Werewolf, Vincent is a Vampire and Izzy is a Keeper. Along with these truths comes the fact that Izzy is in danger.<br /><br />They need to find out what danger and put a stop to it. Come to find out the danger is a lot bigger than they thought.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book and I'm getting ready to start book two myself. I can't wait to read it and find out what else OL has in store for us!</span>

  <span id="freeText11949714122326507453" style="display:none">What a bombshell of a book! This is one paranormal read that left me saying witches, vampires and werewolves... oh my! The Keepers Awakening is not your run of the mill paranormal romance it has kicked it up a notch or two. Lizzy is not your normal average girl she's seen things that make her question her own sanity including the abduction of her mother right before her eyes yet she has no clue as to what or who took her it's all just a blur. Michael enters Lizzy's life and he is a total gentleman that makes Lizzy's heart beat a little faster. The mystery behind this handsome man that can connect with her like no other will leave her on her toes trying to figure out his secret. Vincent drops in unannounced bringing with him a whole whirlwind of information that leaves Lizzy's head spinning all the while releasing a world where the impossible is real. Between the three of them they take us on a paranormal journey like no other I have ever read and I loved it! I want more of The Keepers Series and can't wait to see what author O.L. Ramos has in store for us next! This story pack one heck of a spiced up punch with just a touch of true romantic elements that totally make it a "keeper".<br /><br />Merged review:<br /><br />What a bombshell of a book!         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11139150279270188273">I was given this book in place of an honest review.<br/><br/>I will start by saying that if you read this book have an open mind and be ready to hear a bunch of stuff that you have never heard of before. All the technical stuff in this book just blew my mind. I also had to pick which guy I liked best, I mean you don't have to but I picked mine. I will tell you that this is a book about supernaturals and living in a world that we are just barley living in each day.<br/><br/>This book is mainly about a keeper, werewo</span>
  <span id="freeText11139150279270188273" style="display:none">I was given this book in place of an honest review.<br /><br />I will start by saying that if you read this book have an open mind and be ready to hear a bunch of stuff that you have never heard of before. All the technical stuff in this book just blew my mind. I also had to pick which guy I liked best, I mean you don't have to but I picked mine. I will tell you that this is a book about supernaturals and living in a world that we are just barley living in each day.<br /><br />This book is mainly about a keeper, werewolf, and vampire. I am going against everything I usually pick because vampires are my favorite but this time I am going with Michael the werewolf. There is just something about him that I just can't let go of. I know that Liz has to decide which one she will pick and she feels something different for each one.<br /><br />This book was more than an adventure. There were so many things going on that I stayed excited all the way until the end. The author made sure that I would want to read the next book by the ending in this one. Now I will be going crazy wondering when the next book comes out and what other mysteries I will find out. I am still asking myself questions and I want answers. I can't go and have something not finished.<br /><br />So read this book and join me on my wait and I will have someone else to go crazy with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11139150279270188273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_618375311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/618375311" />
    <a title="Jeannie Zelos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10679154-jeannie-zelos"><img alt="Jeannie Zelos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581157783p2/10679154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/618375311?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeannie Zelos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeannie Zelos" href="/user/show/10679154-jeannie-zelos">Jeannie Zelos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer618375311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer509262984258012443">The Keeper: Awakening (The Keeper Series) O.L. Ramos <br/><br/>I received an ARC in exchange for honest review.<br/><br/>I was contacted by the author and asked to review this book. As usual I looked and read the Amazon sample and decided it was something I'd like to read. Its a very good début book from Mr Ramos and I'd love to read next in the series – hope you don't keep us waiting too long! <br/><br/>It begins with Elizabeth (Liz, Izzy) talking to her therapist about her background. Liz saw her mum taken by something – r</span>
  <span id="freeText509262984258012443" style="display:none">The Keeper: Awakening (The Keeper Series) O.L. Ramos <br /><br />I received an ARC in exchange for honest review.<br /><br />I was contacted by the author and asked to review this book. As usual I looked and read the Amazon sample and decided it was something I'd like to read. Its a very good début book from Mr Ramos and I'd love to read next in the series – hope you don't keep us waiting too long! <br /><br />It begins with Elizabeth (Liz, Izzy) talking to her therapist about her background. Liz saw her mum taken by something – right in front of her in their kitchen but the action was so fast its a blur. Of course no-one believes her and she gained the reputation of being “odd” and she's become a slightly prickly, defensive character. I found her difficult to like at first, she seemed almost aggressive to people. When she first meets Michael (and Vincent later) in the café where she works she's fairly rude to him and if I'd been him I'd have walked out. Still he knows more about her than we do, or than she does herself. The story reveals slowly that there is a supernatural element alive and kicking in the human world and Liz becomes part of it along with Michael and Vincent. There are plots and battles and its a book with a lot of action in. Its not a book to be bored with :) though I felt a little less action and a little more description would have been better. There was a lot of working up to each action scene, but it was over too quickly and I feel it could have been drawn out longer to make it the bigger part of the book it deserved. Still, better than those with pages and pages of dull action, as some books do just to fill pages. <br />The story line was believable, although of course fantasy means suspending belief to a degree there needs to be some form of realism, and I’m always sceptical when the main character such as Liz developers special powers right in the middle of a crisis. Thankfully Liz doesn't and in fact often says how she feels the weak link having nothing special to fight with. I felt it easier to relate to her for that and it made a great change from the novels where the characters are in a battle and the newbie heroine gains powers to save the day ahead of those supernatural who are hundreds, even thousands of years old. I really struggle with that concept.<br />There's a scene at the beginning where she is chatting with Michael about the supernatural world and the possibility of it being real, and Michael says how in history even though there was no contact between people in different countries they've come up with very similar otherworldly creatures – its something that's crossed my mind many times too ;) <br />I liked both Michael and Vincent – more so as time went on and we learned more about them. I like the way they are very different characters with Michael being the planner and Mr responsibility, and Vincent being the fly by the seat of your pants person....Liz was attracted to them both and I can see why – she has a hard decision ahead of her though I think I can see which one its going to be :) but I need next book to tell if I’m right. <br />On the subject of next book – I have a dire horror of cliffhangers – I love series but the recent trend for trilogies with cliffhanger endings leaves me cold and puts me off buying the book as its often months, even a year before we readers learn more by which time the impact has lessened. Mr Ramos doesn't fall into that trap thankfully! The next book is clearly a continuation of this one but though there are lead ins as to what will happen this book of course, the ending to this one is tied up neatly as I'd expect and much in line with conventional series novels – a big Hurrah for that! Hopefully more authors will take note – I know from emails and comments that I’m not alone in HATING cliffhangers, so an end to them will be well supported by many of us. <br />Overall a really excellent first novel and I'd love to read next part. Its excellent value for money at just £2.01 for 282 pages, I have a kind of arbitrary 1.5p per page guideline on the VFM front, and this falls well into that especially as its one to join the keeper files for re reading. <br />Stars: brilliant start -there is room for improvement as with many first novels but I'm giving it a solid four stars. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="509262984258012443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12642124039983366166" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book....getting to know Lizzy, Michael and Vincent was a blast. I understood Lizzy, and could relate to being a loner and feeling like I didn't belong. His immaturity and constant sarcasm truly got on my nerves at first. By the end of the story, I was smitten. I have to say that I loved OL's twist on things, and the way he made me look into his world.   <span id="freeText12740764052611714283" style="display:none">This was a great book.. Truly addicting. I like that OL keeps all the supernaturals that we know and love but also introduces us to something new. A keeper is a new supernatural species to me along with other surprise's that OL adds in the book.<br /><br />Izzy has been trying to find out what took her mother and everyone thinks that she is crazy. Her father is no help since he has become a drunk. She has to see shrink after shrink since everyone thinks that she is crazy. Then she meets Michael.<br /><br />Michael is the first boy that she has ever been attracted to. They eventually start to become close and she tells him about her mother and he is the first person to believe her and not think that she is crazy. Then she meets Vincent.<br /><br />Vincent is rude and sarcastic and Izzy can't seem to figure out why she likes him. Along with meeting Vincent comes the truth. Michael has been keeping secrets and Vincent is all to willing to tell what those are. Michael is a Werewolf, Vincent is a Vampire and Izzy is a Keeper. Along with these truths comes the fact that Izzy is in danger.<br /><br />They need to find out what danger and put a stop to it. Come to find out the danger is a lot bigger than they thought.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book and I'm getting ready to start book two myself. I can't wait to read it and find out what else OL has in store for us!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12273413884529907392">LOVED it and already bought the rest in the series that's out!<br/><br/>Loved the spin of the 'Keeper' in this book along with the usual Vamps and Were's and 'Others'. It kept me turning the pages to see what Lizzy was getting into next and what Michael and Vincent would do to catch her attention and what they would do to keep her safe. This was a well written, thought out book. I really liked Vincent and his blunt sarcastic comments, he made me LOL alot. I didn't know who to root for, him or Michael, and</span>
  <span id="freeText12273413884529907392" style="display:none">LOVED it and already bought the rest in the series that's out!<br /><br />Loved the spin of the 'Keeper' in this book along with the usual Vamps and Were's and 'Others'. It kept me turning the pages to see what Lizzy was getting into next and what Michael and Vincent would do to catch her attention and what they would do to keep her safe. This was a well written, thought out book. I really liked Vincent and his blunt sarcastic comments, he made me LOL alot. I didn't know who to root for, him or Michael, and still don't!! :) As soon as I finished reading this book I was already looking for the next in the series and then purchased them all so I can continue the Saga. There are a couple spots that you really feel a YA vibe from, cause LIzzy is only 19 and she acts it, BUT you won't be disappointed with this read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11014217909196929308">What an incredible read. After reading many Paranormal books, sometimes the genre can get stale. Mr. Ramos has refreshed and added to! The characters are very specific and relatable,Vincent is my favorite. The story is packed with great fight scenes. The plot has some very interesting twists and turns and kept involved and interested the entire time. Also, Mr. Ramos has added a NEW paranormal Species that I, for one, have never heard of. The book is well written and flows easily.<br/><br/>I am a huge new </span>
  <span id="freeText11014217909196929308" style="display:none">What an incredible read. After reading many Paranormal books, sometimes the genre can get stale. Mr. Ramos has refreshed and added to! The characters are very specific and relatable,Vincent is my favorite. The story is packed with great fight scenes. The plot has some very interesting twists and turns and kept involved and interested the entire time. Also, Mr. Ramos has added a NEW paranormal Species that I, for one, have never heard of. The book is well written and flows easily.<br /><br />I am a huge new fan and will be definitely buying the next one.</span>

<div id="review_637502550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637502550" />
    <a title="Rachel V." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7429855-rachel-v"><img alt="Rachel V." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333507299p2/7429855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637502550?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel V." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel V." href="/user/show/7429855-rachel-v">Rachel V.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781484857069" href="/book/show/17950269-awakening">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7429855-rachel-v?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637502550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4683654994278863293">There is finally a new supernatural creature introduced into paranormal books. I am excited! This new creature is a Keeper. What is that you may ask? Well you will have to read the book to find out. I am not going to spoil it. The author combines old supernatural creatures in this book with ones we have never seen giving it a new view point and a twist to old ideas. The plot is certainly unique also with new ideas popping up everywhere. I give this one 3.5 stars.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed Vincenzo’s sense</span>
  <span id="freeText4683654994278863293" style="display:none">There is finally a new supernatural creature introduced into paranormal books. I am excited! This new creature is a Keeper. What is that you may ask? Well you will have to read the book to find out. I am not going to spoil it. The author combines old supernatural creatures in this book with ones we have never seen giving it a new view point and a twist to old ideas. The plot is certainly unique also with new ideas popping up everywhere. I give this one 3.5 stars.<br /><br />I really enjoyed Vincenzo’s sense of humor and Michael’s seriousness. These two really work well together as a team as well as complement each other with their differences. Elizabeth is a college student whose IQ is way above average. She is convinced that something supernatural took her mother when she was a child but nobody believes her. It has destroyed her family. The author did a really great job of characterization. I really feel that I know these characters.<br /><br />The only problem I had with this story was the writing. It wasn’t a style that I liked quite as much as others. I felt more like I was being told as opposed to being shown what was happening with in the story. Elizabeth did get on my nerves at times too. It was more her personality and her inner dialogue. She seemed so clueless and also at time like she herself was a contradiction. She was helpless and confused one minute then strong the next.<br /><br />That being said I would read the next book in this series. The plot alone is one that I would like to follow and I am curious if the writing style may evolve into something that I may like better down the road. I am curious to know how it turns out for these three main characters.<br /><br />*I received a copy of this book free from author in exchange for an honest opinion.*</span>
  <a data-text-id="4683654994278863293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gpxTGmbG24ntYC9aCAGXR7fVSn1gtKfnCHHAKCvTAMTr8D8ITIsUWlhC6+gYN3Y7nCyKeEKg2NRlB4VfQYzBdQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('srUYMCW2ZW0Fd3c3eTPYNgG0CLKpvBdLmzEFoSrf2kvb2XQiD/uqvrBVs4VpBTlKKk3It4uoaHj2R0DWQIAb+g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

While this has had the positive effect of equalizing access to knowledge, it also has lowered the bar on what depth of knowledge is required t<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9560046028801577431\" style=\"display:none\">The rise of the internet and other technology has made information more easily-accessible than ever before. While this has had the positive effect of equalizing access to knowledge, it also has lowered the bar on what depth of knowledge is required to consider oneself an &quot;expert.&quot; A cult of anti-expertise sentiment has coincided with anti-intellectualism, resulting in massively viral yet poorly informed debates ranging from the anti-vaccination movement to attacks on GMOs. This surge in intellectual egalitarianism has altered the landscape of debates-all voices are equal, and &quot;fact&quot; is a subjective term. Browsing WebMD puts one on equal footing with doctors, and Wikipedia allows all to be foreign policy experts, scientists, and more. As Tom Nichols shows in The Death of Expertise, there are a number of reasons why this has occurred-ranging from easy access to Internet search engines to a customer satisfaction model within higher education. The product of these interrelated trends, Nichols argues, is a pervasive distrust of expertise among the public coinciding with an unfounded belief among non-experts that their opinions should have equal standing with those of the experts. The experts are not always right, of course, and Nichols discusses expert failure. The crucial point is that bad decisions by experts can and have been effectively challenged by other well-informed experts. The issue now is that the democratization of information dissemination has created an army of ill-informed citizens who denounce expertise.\n\nWhen challenged, non-experts resort to the false argument that the experts are often wrong. Though it may be true, but the solution is not to jettison expertise as an ideal; it is to improve our expertise. Nichols is certainly not opposed to information democratization, but rather the enlightenment people believe they achieve after superficial internet research. He shows in vivid detail the ways in which this impulse is coursing through our culture and body politic, but the larger goal is to explain the benefits that expertise and rigorous learning regimes bestow upon all societies.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"9560046028801577431\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div In Facts and Fears Clapper traces his career through his rise in ranks of the military, the history of several decades of national intelligence operations, the growing threat of cyberattacks, his relationships with presidents and Congress, and the truth about Russia\'s role in the presidential election. He describes, in the wake of Snowden and WikiLeaks, his efforts to make intelligence more transparent and to push back against the suspicion that Americans\' private lives are subject to surveillance. \n\nClapper considers such difficult questions as, is intelligence ethical? So when she gets a job offer in the middle of nowhere, Zoe jumps at the chance to make a name for herself only to find her new home is teeming with magic and paranormal beings—and those aren\'t its only secrets.  During a heated election for Head Witch, the most powerful position in town, Zoe’s predecessor was buried alive—and accusations are flying faster than broomsticks. Despite her editor’s orders to leave the story alone, Zoe can’t resist.  From the front-running witch with a secret to the mysterious vampires pulling strings in the shadows, Zoe knows the truth is just under the surface. So after she discovers she has rare telepathic abilities, Zoe realizes she\'s the only one who can keep digging.  Will Zoe’s powers lead her to the murderer and the scoop of a lifetime? Or will they send her to an early grave?  &#x2028;&#x2028;Spellbooks and Stakings, Book 2:&#x2028;&#x2028;  Zoe Clarke is going back to school. After learning she’s telepathic and risking her life to solve a paranormal murder, she’s been invited to the prestigious Veilside Academy of Magic to sharpen her newfound powers.  But not all the students are spellbound by Zoe, and it isn’t long before she realizes the Academy is brimming with exceptional witches and warlocks—who are as cutthroat as they are talented.  So when Zoe’s new favorite vampire professor is found in a pile of ash, all spell breaks loose.  Between troublemaking witches and a jealous staff, Zoe knows whoever the murderer is, they aren’t finished handing out suspensions.  Can Zoe work her magic to reveal the killer? Or will she fail the ultimate test?&#x2028;&#x2028;  Alchemy and Arson, Book 3:  &#x2028;&#x2028;Zoe Clarke’s life just keeps getting better. After repeatedly risking her life to solve a rash of paranormal murders in Moon Grove, Zoe’s become a household name.  But her newfound attention isn’t all magic. Zoe knows she’s made enemies along the way and that they aren’t above pouring gas on her troubles.  So when one of Moon Grove’s most prominent witches dies in an inexplicable house fire, hysteria ignites—and Zoe finds herself standing in the ashes.  From the psychedelic new alchemist in town to the werewolves running shady businesses, Zoe’s certain someone’s trying to torch her reputation. And when another building spontaneously combusts, Zoe knows she’ll have to walk through fire and brimstone to stop the arsonist.  Can Zoe stamp out the killer before they strike again? Or will she go up in flames?
